  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b105a987-7f03-41f4-924b-8afaf7239b62'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer12659439823152239154">Roanna Davenport was raised a wealthy orphan on her grandmother's magnificent Alabama estate, Davencourt, where she had a passion for horses, a genius for trouble, and a deep love for her cousin, Webb. But everyone expected Webb to marry their ravishing cousin, Jessie. When he did, Roanna's desire became no more than the stuff of dreams -- until the night Jessie was found </span>
  <span id="freeText12659439823152239154" style="display:none">Roanna Davenport was raised a wealthy orphan on her grandmother's magnificent Alabama estate, Davencourt, where she had a passion for horses, a genius for trouble, and a deep love for her cousin, Webb. But everyone expected Webb to marry their ravishing cousin, Jessie. When he did, Roanna's desire became no more than the stuff of dreams -- until the night Jessie was found bludgeoned to death. <br /> After the shocking murder of his wife, Webb left for Arizona, abandoning the legacy that he had once believed was all he wanted. But then an all-grown-up Roanna walked into a dingy bar in Nogales to bring him home; the mischievous sprite he had known ten years earlier was no more. Gone, too, was her fire. In its place was ice that melted at his touch. Webb is drawn back to Davencourt, to Roanna, and to the killer that once destroyed his life and waits only for the chance to finish the job....</span>
  <a data-text-id="12659439823152239154" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3488873265" class="readable"

<div id="review_785169775" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/785169775" />
    <a title="Sophie ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14918997-sophie"><img alt="Sophie ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374051209p2/14918997.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/785169775?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie ♥" href="/user/show/14918997-sophie">Sophie ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Romantic suspense fans, Linda Howard fans, those who enjoyed After the Night in particular!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14918997-sophie?shelf=ebooks-i-own">ebooks-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14918997-sophie?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14918997-sophie?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14918997-sophie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14918997-sophie?shelf=second-chance-love">second-chance-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14918997-sophie?shelf=my-reviews">my-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14918997-sophie?shelf=contemp-romance">contemp-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer785169775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10254085796974877498"><b>WARNING: Fragile Heroine Ahead</b><br/><br/><b>☆☆☆☆☆☆☆☆☆☆<br/>10 STARS FOR THIS MASTERPIECE BY LINDA HOWARD - I AM HEAD OVER HEELS IN LOVE WITH THIS I CAN'T EVEN...ROANNA WAS A 100% PERFECT HEROINE</b><br/><br/>I am finally out of my reading rut. Hurrah! All those historical romances and mellow contemporaries finally got to me and I was definitely in the mood to shake it up a bit so I decided to make another venture into romantic suspense and I just cannot believe how hard I fell for this book. What really skyrocketed this book up</span>
  <span id="freeText10254085796974877498" style="display:none"><b>WARNING: Fragile Heroine Ahead</b><br /><br /><b>☆☆☆☆☆☆☆☆☆☆<br />10 STARS FOR THIS MASTERPIECE BY LINDA HOWARD - I AM HEAD OVER HEELS IN LOVE WITH THIS I CAN'T EVEN...ROANNA WAS A 100% PERFECT HEROINE</b><br /><br />I am finally out of my reading rut. Hurrah! All those historical romances and mellow contemporaries finally got to me and I was definitely in the mood to shake it up a bit so I decided to make another venture into romantic suspense and I just cannot believe how hard I fell for this book. What really skyrocketed this book up my favourites list was definitely the heroine Roanna. She was <i>fabulous</i>. It's been no secret that I prefer delicate heroines (who are strong in their own way) over wilful sharp-tongued ones. Linda Howard just created my ideal heroine.<br /><br />As a child, Roanna was the adoring admirer of Webb, husband-to-be of her evil, disgusting, despicable (every nasty word in the dictionary) sister Jesse. Her death honestly didn't come soon enough! Roanna is the sweet innocent child, unloved and left on the sidelines as Jesse bullies her into losing all her self-esteem. As the years run by, Jesse marries Webb and leaves her longing for a love that could never have been. After Jesse's abrupt death, Roanna and Webb are torn apart as Webb disappears for ten years. The family initally accuse Roanna of killing Jesse before turning the finger of blame on Webb. A single act of rejection from Web starts Roanna's transformaiton into a softly-spoken, tightly controlled woman.<br /><br />But then Webb comes back. Yayayay and the fun part of the book begins. Roanna, despite her carefully constructed protective shell is still painfully vulnerable when it comes to Webb. This, for me, really set this book up as one of my absolute faves. I cannot stand it when the heroines develops a 'fuck you' attitude towards the man they love after seeing them for the first time after ten years and turns into a prickly porcupine/shrew who then melts out of their panties at the mere thought of sex. Honestly. Im so over the whole playing hard to get crap which is exactly why this book hit the right notes with me. I loved how Roanna didn't even pretend she was over Webb. Instead he worked hard to rebuild her self-esteem after seeing her vulnerability and there is actually character development instead of just 'mindless fucking'! Whoo three cheers for old school love!!!<br /><br />Even though this wasn't 'historical romance' in its purest sense it is set a few decades back and the Davenport family dynamics are startingly unique. I won't spoil it for you, but at the risk of sounding terrible naive and sheltered, I thought some of the things in this book were slightly confronting. Oh yes, and don't be put off by the fact Webb and Roanna are second cousins. In the grand scheme of things it didn't really bother me (I just pretended they weren't which worked for me).<br /><br />This one is going into my favourites for sure... As for the rest of Linda Howard's books... WATCH OUT HERE I COME. I've officially fallen in love with romantic suspense too. Haha never thought I'd say that. It makes sense though - my all time favourite book is a romantic suspense. I can't believe I haven't read much of the genre though! Go and get this book guys - definitely worth your while!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10254085796974877498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10678416213933469853" style="display:none">I’ll keep this one short and sweet.<br><br>I guess you could say that I enjoyed Shades of Twilight. It is apparent by my updates. But in the end this one settled around the 3.5 – 4 stars rating.     <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1773478413?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=kissing-books">kissing-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1773478413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1437037862537451225"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>I <i>love </i>challenges, and that's why the mods and I at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/photo/group/187063-unapologetic-romance-readers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Unapologetic Romance Readers</a> came up with the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/13932464-halloween-2016-reading-challenge' rel='nofollow noopener'>Halloween 2016 Reading Challenge</a>. We're shining the light on the darker side of romance and seeing what horrible, creepy things come a-crawling out. I picked SHADES OF TWILIGHT to satisfy the "romance involving a murder" category, and boy, did it satisfy on that end.<br/><br/><br/><br/>SHADES OF TWILIGHT features Roanna Davenport, one of the heirs to a wealthy </span>
  <span id="freeText1437037862537451225" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>I <i>love </i>challenges, and that's why the mods and I at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/photo/group/187063-unapologetic-romance-readers" rel="nofollow noopener">Unapologetic Romance Readers</a> came up with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/13932464-halloween-2016-reading-challenge" rel="nofollow noopener">Halloween 2016 Reading Challenge</a>. We're shining the light on the darker side of romance and seeing what horrible, creepy things come a-crawling out. I picked SHADES OF TWILIGHT to satisfy the "romance involving a murder" category, and boy, did it satisfy on that end.<br><br><br><br>SHADES OF TWILIGHT features Roanna Davenport, one of the heirs to a wealthy Alabama family. When her parents and aunt die in a tragic accident, both she and her cousin Jessie are left orphans, and forced to live at the intimidating Davencourt mansion with the stern family matriarch, Lucinda, for whom honor is everything.<br><br><br><br>Jessie is beautiful, cold, and cruel - and even though she always gets whatever she wants, she hates Roanna for some reason and isn't afraid to show it every chance she gets. Heaping on abuse, making nasty comments, showing petty slights; Jessie isn't above anything to put Roanna down. For some reason, the other family members tolerate - or even encourage - this emotional abuse. The only person in Roanna's corner is the handsome Webb, her second cousin who is seven years older than she is. Roanna has a huge crush on him, and she's upset that even though he shows her affection, he is attracted to Jessie like everyone else and plans to marry her.<br><br><br><br>When Roanna is seventeen, Davencourt is stuffed full of Davenports and Tallants. She can't do any right, and seeks refuge with her horses  - and with Webb, who is now married to Jessie. Roanna wants Webb more than ever and is secretly happy that their marriage is failing. Then, one day, she catches Jessie sleeping with a man who isn't her husband,  and later forces herself on Webb. Jessie catches them kissing and raises a scene that brings all the family members running. A major fight breaks out. And then, later that night, Jessie turns up dead. Death by fire poker. Natural causes, obviously. Just kidding, it's murder and everyone assumes Webb does it, which is why he skips town. Roanna doesn't lay eyes on him again for another ten years when her grandmother Lucinda employs her to seek him out and find him and bring him back to Davencourt to assume his role as rightful heir.<br><br><br><br>With its bad sex, family drama, and sexist hero themes, this is 90s cheese at its cheesiest and normally I spread that on crackers and snarf it down like there's no tomorrow, but I took a lot of issues with SHADES OF TWILIGHT and I just couldn't put them aside.<br><br><br><br>Problem #1: The incest. I don't know what it is about this week, you guys, but this is the <i>third </i>book I've picked up this week that had incest in it. I thought COVENANT WITH THE VAMPIRE couldn't be topped in grossness, but I was wrong. So, so wrong.<br><br><br><br>Problem #2: The characters. Everyone in this book actively takes their vitamin D-bag supplements; there isn't a single likable character to be found within these pages. If the person in question isn't an outright psycho or b*tch, they're an emotionally insensitive, self-centered puckerhole, with the sensitivity of a lead pipe. Even the characters I was supposed to like, like Webb and Roanna, annoyed me. Webb is one of those overbearing alpha cavemen who tell the heroine how and well to eat and get so caught up in their passions that they "accidentally" forget to wear condoms. Roanna was awful because she's the definition of a doormat. In fact, if you look hard, you can still sort of make out the faded "welcome" on her forehead. All she does is cry and mope. Her character flaws are that she sleepwalks and that she doesn't eat when she's upset - which is all the freaking time.<br><br><br><br>Problem #3: The way eating disorders are broached in this book. It's hinted that Roanna might have anorexia. At the very least, she has an emotional-related eating disorder, because whenever she's anxious, upset, or guilty, she doesn't eat. Her attitude toward food really made me uncomfortable in this book. We're constantly told how skinny Roanna is and not necessarily in a bad way - she's compared to dolls or called child-like. Webb marvels that seventeen year old Roanna seems to weigh the same amount as seven year old Roanna. At one point in the story she gets so upset that she stops eating entirely and goes down to 80lbs (at 5'7"), and nearly dies. She calls eating a "chore" several times, and the hero admires her narrow hips, small breasts, and flat stomach on several occasions. We're told, several times, exactly how much weight Roanna can stand to gain (15lbs). When Webb actually gets romantically involved with her (and even before then), he starts trying to control her diet. This felt so unnecessary to the storyline and yet was such an integral part of it, that it felt odd. I'm not against skinny women and I do think it's important to raise awareness of eating disorders in fiction, but the way it was presented in this book created a lot of uncomfortable mixed signals.<br><br><br><br>Problem #4: The way sex is broached in this book. It's the 90s. Romance novels then were a very different animal from the ones in today's market place. Men had mats of chest hair and women were always virginal. But the slut-shaming is strong in this one. It's very important that Webb compare the differences between Jessie and Roanna once he starts sleeping with Roanna. It's important that Roanna have "uncomplicated sensuality" (or something like that) and that she doesn't use sex for power or manipulation. At one point he marvels at her virginal virginity, saying that if she didn't go horseback riding, he probably wouldn't have even been able to get a finger in her. I'm sorry, but at what point did the female anatomy become tantamount to a Chinese fingertrap? Vaginas do not work that way. Here, I'm not even going to say anymore on this. I'm just going to direct you to this awesome movie done by Adam Connover called "<a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PM79UBTwfsg" rel="nofollow noopener">The Truth About Hymens and Sex</a>."<br><br><br><br>But as much as this book annoyed me, I didn't hate SHADES OF TWILIGHT. The first 100 pages were excellent and made me think that I had a 4-star read on my hand. The problem was that in her quest to make Roanna a sympathetic character, the author made her an utterly unlikable one, because she lacked any sort of goals or internal conflict apart from "But I want Webb to like me!" It's a shame because I really liked the setup and I'm usually a sucker for small-town intrigues like these. Take this book from Sandra Brown's backlist, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30346.Slow_Heat_in_Heaven?from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">SLOW HEAT IN HEAVEN</a>. It follows a very similar formula, but the mystery is more engaging and the heroine is a little less...sad. When the hero and heroine butt heads in SLOW HEAT, it feels less like victimization and more like a fight between equals.<br><br><br><br>2 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1437037862537451225" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      <a href="/user/show/14918997-sophie">Sophie ♥</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=angst-in-my-pants">angst-in-my-pants</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=friends-to-lovers">friends-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=betrayal">betrayal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=tragic-loss">tragic-loss</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer817941393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12264795430202504233">~~~~~~ 4.5 STARS! ~~~~~~<br/><br/>Wow. Linda Howard is quickly becoming one of my fave authors. <br/><br/>This book was so consuming, so thorough in its ability to make me cry, hate, despair and feel joy. It had a very epic feel to it although the events transcend 20 years in total. I loved the characters, even the bad ones. Roanna was a girl that lost her parents as a child only to live with her grandmother at Davencourt, the estate her father's family established.<br/>She's also loved her second cousin, Webb---this di</span>
  <span id="freeText12264795430202504233" style="display:none">~~~~~~ 4.5 STARS! ~~~~~~<br /><br />Wow. Linda Howard is quickly becoming one of my fave authors. <br /><br />This book was so consuming, so thorough in its ability to make me cry, hate, despair and feel joy. It had a very epic feel to it although the events transcend 20 years in total. I loved the characters, even the bad ones. Roanna was a girl that lost her parents as a child only to live with her grandmother at Davencourt, the estate her father's family established.<br />She's also loved her second cousin, Webb---this didn't disturb me at all---for as long as she remembers. But Webb is slated to take up the reigns of Davencourt, and will also marry his second cousin, Jessie, first cousin and nemesis to Roanna. But eventually tragedy strikes Davencourt, forcing Webb to abandon his hold on it and everyone in it, including Roanna. The book is divided into 3 parts: The three as children, then as young adults and finally as adults. <br /><br />I really liked Roanna and empathized with her as a child then as a woman very different from who she used to be. She's grown cold and remote, hiding her feelings under layers of ice. Her only weakness is and will always be Webb. When she seeks him out requesting he return home, Webb can't believe the fine woman she's become. But she also ignites his long buried feelings of abandonment and he says some pretty vicious things. But Roanna loves him beyond reason and brings him home, the prodigal son, if you may.<br /><br />The romance was a nice slow build that explodes between two people holding their feelings in restraint. Webb and Roanna are so similar and feel so strongly for each other that it became frustrating for me waiting for them to finally act on their desires. The suspense was fantastic and I was honestly stumped till the bitter end. The person I thought responsible was soon eradicated from my list and I found myself mystified by who actually committed the crime. <br /><br />That raw sensuality I've come to correlate with LH's writing was here once more. She writes love scenes on such an intimate level. There's no over the top smexy time that seems orchestrated, there's no derogatory expletives used to induce orgasm....it's just a sensuality I don't see often enough, making me wish authors were more attuned to the importance of that.<br /><br />OBVIOUSLY I will continue reading LH's other works! Sometimes you think an older book or an author being around for years won't deliver. You might think there'll be too much fade to black scenes or old fashioned ideas...Well, I'm never abiding by that ridiculous notion again. These books may have been around for years but they have the advantage of longevity because they're written so well the stories become timeless. Loved this.<br /><br />Thanks for the rec Sophie! xx<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12264795430202504233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_120052630" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/120052630" />
    <a title="Jane Stewart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart"><img alt="Jane Stewart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346001994p2/3789528.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/120052630?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane Stewart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane Stewart" href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart">Jane Stewart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3789528-jane-stewart?shelf=contemporary-romantic-suspense">contemporary-romantic-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120052630" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer869154499500031775">I love this author, but I don't recommend this book. Roanna lost her parents at age 7.<br/><br/>She then lived with an evil cousin Jessie who bullied and tormented her constantly for 10 years. Jessie was killed and the relatives at first believed Roanna did it, then later believed Webb did it so he left town for 10 years. He made erroneous assumptions about Roanna and acted like he hated her as he left. He was the only one who cared for her and raised her from age 7, and she felt abandoned. Other relative</span>
  <span id="freeText869154499500031775" style="display:none">I love this author, but I don't recommend this book. Roanna lost her parents at age 7.<br /><br />She then lived with an evil cousin Jessie who bullied and tormented her constantly for 10 years. Jessie was killed and the relatives at first believed Roanna did it, then later believed Webb did it so he left town for 10 years. He made erroneous assumptions about Roanna and acted like he hated her as he left. He was the only one who cared for her and raised her from age 7, and she felt abandoned. Other relatives came to live in the house with Roanna and treated her badly for the next 10 years. I have four problems with this book. First, Roanna was too much of a victim and everyone else contributed to it. The grandmother should have done more to protect and help Roanna, especially when Roanna was initially accused of the murder by the relatives. I did not enjoy having the majority of the story dealing with the sadness, grief and helplessness of this victim. My second complaint is that Roanna and Webb both lusted for and loved each other but they stayed away from each other due to making wrong assumptions. He felt like he forced sex on her, and said it wouldn't happen again. She thought he didn't like sex with her and didn't want her anymore so she said she understood and that she would leave him alone. He said you don't understand anything, but he didn't clarify. She thought he didn't want her. I don't know why he continued to stay away from her. This went on for most of the book. She was honest in her communication, but he was not. Finally when they did get together he said "I've tried to stay away from you." She said "Why." He said "God knows." Later he said "I thought I was being noble by not taking advantage of you." I never did understand his reasons. He should not have stayed away from her like that and should have been more direct in his communication with her. Third, the author spent too much time inside Roanna's head, thinking and worrying about things. Many of these worries were based on erroneous assumptions or could have been solved. Some of this bored me. Fourth, I was confused about cousins who shared the same grandmother being able to marry and produce offspring with genetic safety. This sounded like they were too closedly related to me, but I'm not familiar enough with genetics to know. Sexual language: moderate. Number of sex scenes: nine. Setting: 1990s Alabama. Copyright: 1996. Genre: contemporary romantic suspense.</span>
  <a data-text-id="869154499500031775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I really cannot wrap my head around that.<br /> <br />Of course these two fucktards aren't the main couple but I don't care. I really don't. <span id="freeTextContainer17602677803279170903"><br/>Reread and reviewed on: 9.25.20<br/><br/><i>
  <b>4 Southern Suspense Stars!! </b>
</i><br/><br/>I first read this book many years ago. It is just as good today as then, and it is one of the major reasons I remain a devoted fan of Linda Howards back list. Her suspense, southern families, wealth, greed, and a good mystery....along with a strong Alpha Male and a sensual love that we come to expect from a LH book. <br/><br/><a href='https://app.photobucket.com/u/dshewey1/a/39cfee4e-53fe-4277-af3c-70867c33051e/p/665604aa-100c-489f-a093-b6bf4361bb6d' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1601122159i/30155727.jpg' alt='6185D369_6C23_4BA7_A89C_9A91A1FB3C21' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/>Cousins Jessie and Roanna Davenport both lose their parents in a auto accident as a young children and are now livi</span>
  <span id="freeText17602677803279170903" style="display:none"><br>Reread and reviewed on: 9.25.20<br><br><i>
  <b>4 Southern Suspense Stars!! </b>
</i><br><br>I first read this book many years ago. It is just as good today as then, and it is one of the major reasons I remain a devoted fan of Linda Howards back list. Her suspense, southern families, wealth, greed, and a good mystery....along with a strong Alpha Male and a sensual love that we come to expect from a LH book. <br><br><a href="https://app.photobucket.com/u/dshewey1/a/39cfee4e-53fe-4277-af3c-70867c33051e/p/665604aa-100c-489f-a093-b6bf4361bb6d" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1601122159i/30155727.jpg" alt="6185D369_6C23_4BA7_A89C_9A91A1FB3C21" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>Cousins Jessie and Roanna Davenport both lose their parents in a auto accident as a young children and are now living with their Grandmother, Patriarch of the Davenport family Lucinda Davenport. There young Roanna meets and falls in love with her distant cousin, Webb Tallant. First she hero-worships him as a child and then as an adolescent she has a teenage crush on him. However, Webb was always destined to marry another cousin, the beautiful but tempestous Jessie. The wedding goes as planned but when Jessie is found murdered one evening in her bedroom all fingers point towards Webb. Webb decides to leave the family because of the lack of support when he needed it most. Webb decides to leave Alabama and heads to Arizona.<br><br>Ten years pass and Roanna is now grown up and Lucinda is dying. Lucinda's dying wish is for her beloved Webb to return to the family home and to take his rightful place and take over as heir apparent over the Davenport empire. Roanna heads to Arizona to persuade Webb to return home. Webb finally decides to return with her but tongues start wagging and old gossip and suspicions are renewed. With Webb's return, Roanna starts receiving new threats. Is Jessie's killer still a danger to the Davenport/Tallant family? Will Webb ever return Roanna's unrequited love? <br><br>I highly recommend this book...if you haven't read a Linda Howard book, then you are in for a delicious treat.<br><br><i>*Original read May 2011</i></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LibraryLass" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LibraryLass" href="/user/show/882302-librarylass">LibraryLass</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50095713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13630089285090237247">4.5 stars for this one. I usually am not into the 'family drama' type scenario in books esp. if they have 1/2 a book in the past and 1/2 in the now - BUT this one grabbed me right from the prologue and I had difficulty putting it down (therefore I did so very rarely ;)<br/><br/>I loved Roanna and Webb. The only reason this didn't get a full 5 stars though, was that I think Roanna's love for Webb was at times a bit wimpy. Having said that, I thoroughly enjoyed their interaction. Unlike other reviewers I di</span>
  <span id="freeText13630089285090237247" style="display:none">4.5 stars for this one. I usually am not into the 'family drama' type scenario in books esp. if they have 1/2 a book in the past and 1/2 in the now - BUT this one grabbed me right from the prologue and I had difficulty putting it down (therefore I did so very rarely ;)<br /><br />I loved Roanna and Webb. The only reason this didn't get a full 5 stars though, was that I think Roanna's love for Webb was at times a bit wimpy. Having said that, I thoroughly enjoyed their interaction. Unlike other reviewers I didn't find Roanna too vulnerable...I think LH portrayed Roanna and her shut-off feelings extremely well. I also like the fact that when Webb came back on the scene, there was no magic wand and Roanna was all better. I LIKED the fragility of Roanna and I thought Webb's growing realisation of his real feelings for her were fantastic. And of course the sex was hot, hot, hot!<br /><br />Yes there were some seriously uncomfortable moments in the book with some of the subject matter, however, this in fact added to the book not subtracted from it. <br /><br />This was a stand out for me. HIghly recommended to everyone. (But if you like your heroines kick-ass this might not be for you even though Roanna was a kick-ass in her own way)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer323890273295670191">3.5 rounded up.<br/><br/>This definitely kept me interested, although I could have done without graphic sex scenes between secondary characters. <b>**Trigger warning</b> for incest.<br/><br/>This book starts when the h is 7 and ends when she's 27, two decades are glossed over, but it's primarily the story of how Roanna survived and grew/changed over the years.<br/><br/>The hero is 5-6 years older and Roanna's 2nd cousin. She lives under the same roof with him from 7 to 17, during which time she goes from big brother/hero worship to</span>
  <span id="freeText323890273295670191" style="display:none">3.5 rounded up.<br /><br />This definitely kept me interested, although I could have done without graphic sex scenes between secondary characters. <b>**Trigger warning</b> for incest.<br /><br />This book starts when the h is 7 and ends when she's 27, two decades are glossed over, but it's primarily the story of how Roanna survived and grew/changed over the years.<br /><br />The hero is 5-6 years older and Roanna's 2nd cousin. She lives under the same roof with him from 7 to 17, during which time she goes from big brother/hero worship to more romantic feelings. I didn't get an incesty vibe from that, but some may be bothered - especially since he marries another cousin first (this is not the trigger warning I spoke of).<br /><br />There are some interesting secondary characters, like the h's grandmother and family matriarch who you will likely hate at first and only appreciate later. The family dynamics are also interesting and a bit twisted at times.<br /><br />A suspense and a murder mystery is the big event which ties the book together. However, as I said before, I think this is primarily about the h growing (very painfully at times) into someone who saw herself as worthy.</span>

<div id="review_837066287" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/837066287" />
    <a title="Carol Storm" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5032322-carol-storm"><img alt="Carol Storm" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442507712p2/5032322.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/837066287?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol Storm" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol Storm" href="/user/show/5032322-carol-storm">Carol Storm</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780671799373" href="/book/show/2167503.Shades_of_Twilight">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer837066287" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3547940424947875887">This was an amazing book! More than a romance novel, it's a literary work that celebrates the American south and shows its darker side with all the sizzling intensity of Tennessee Williams.<br/><br/>Roanna Davenport is the most original heroine I've ever seen in a contemporary romance novel. So often in reviews we say someone (usually the hero) is "wild." And people just use "wild" to mean vibrant, sexy, passionate, whatever. But what makes Roanna so heartbreaking and original is that she really is . . . </span>
  <span id="freeText3547940424947875887" style="display:none">This was an amazing book! More than a romance novel, it's a literary work that celebrates the American south and shows its darker side with all the sizzling intensity of Tennessee Williams.<br /><br />Roanna Davenport is the most original heroine I've ever seen in a contemporary romance novel. So often in reviews we say someone (usually the hero) is "wild." And people just use "wild" to mean vibrant, sexy, passionate, whatever. But what makes Roanna so heartbreaking and original is that she really is . . . wild. As in a helpless wild creature that's abandoned by its parents, more like an animal than a person in many ways. Roanna has no real feelings of trust towards any of the wealthy people who take her in and give her a home. She's almost like a different species from them.<br /><br />The only person who can reach her is Webb. And Webb is like a young prince, a southern equivalent of the favored heir to a dukedom. How he makes time for this wild, tormented young girl is so touching, and when a vicious, scheming, unforgettably evil vixen comes between them it doesn't seem fake at all. It seems incredibly real and heartbreaking.<br /><br />Webb is such an amazing hero. Not because he's strong and handsome and rich. And not because he turns his back on his Alabama wealth and makes even more money as a rancher. And certainly not because he "hunts down rustlers single-handed." (Puh-leeze!) What makes him special is that when he returns home and sees the shy, cultivated, isolated young woman Roanna has become, he's determined to bring her out of her shell. To make her smile. To bring laughter back into her life. How many romance novels have you read where the hero literally counts the times he can make the heroine smile? I found that so inspiring and so romantic.<br /><br />Sophie on Goodreads recommended this book to me, and all I have to say is thank you, thank you, thank you!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3547940424947875887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1593196257" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46841583-chitra-cj?shelf=heroines-i-love">heroines-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46841583-chitra-cj?shelf=tearjerker">tearjerker</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46841583-chitra-cj?shelf=seduced-by-the-sex">seduced-by-the-sex</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46841583-chitra-cj?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46841583-chitra-cj?shelf=v-card">v-card</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1593196257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9131451058403522829"><i> <b> "I loved you when you were a snot-nosed kid, into so much mischief it's a wonder my hair didn't turn prematurely gray. I loved you when you were a teenager with long, skinny legs and eyes that broke my heart every time I looked at you. I love you now that you're a woman who makes my brain go soft, my legs go weak, and my dick get hard. When you walk into a room, my heart damn near jumps out of my chest. When you smile, I feel as if I've won a Nobel Prize. And your eyes still break my heart." </b></i><br/><br/>O</span>
  <span id="freeText9131451058403522829" style="display:none"><i> <b> "I loved you when you were a snot-nosed kid, into so much mischief it's a wonder my hair didn't turn prematurely gray. I loved you when you were a teenager with long, skinny legs and eyes that broke my heart every time I looked at you. I love you now that you're a woman who makes my brain go soft, my legs go weak, and my dick get hard. When you walk into a room, my heart damn near jumps out of my chest. When you smile, I feel as if I've won a Nobel Prize. And your eyes still break my heart." </b></i><br /><br />Oh my god..WOW!<br />So finally after putting off this book for two years, I decided to read it in occasion of completing my GR 2016 challenge.<br />And it was amazing.<br />The suspense filled love story of Roanne and Webb captures you from page one and then proceeds to take you on a roller coaster ride.<br />Roanne has always loved her second cousin Webb, even when he chose the prettier cousin Jessie and later marries her.<br />When Jessie is murdered, and misunderstandings make Webb leave- ten years later it's on Ro to bring him back for sake of their sick grandmother Lucinda. And she does. And mysteries unravel.<br />I LOVED ROANNE. I MEAN LOVED LOVED LOVED. Her quiet intensity, her unending devotion and love, and her ability to bear everything with a stride just stole my heart. I cried every time she had her heart trampled, ridiculed and pushed in- but she never gave up and kept going on. She loved Webb, and stood with it. She will totally go into one of my all time favorite heroines. <br />Webb on the other hand was initially an ambitious hero, to later a righteous and recovering man.<br />Going from an angsty widower, to a hero who falls in love- it was lovely to see his character evolving and falling hard.<br />This book had a heavy dose of angst- which I again LOVED and of murder and betrayal.<br />What happens that fateful night changes the course of the story, however Roanne and Webb continue to be the center of story.<br />Side characters like Lucinda, Loyal, etc play their parts well, and you hate and adore in equal parts.<br />The love making scenes are scorchingly HOT, and worth rereading.<br />However, this book might annoy some people who might not like<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />-Descriptive sex scenes of other characters<br />-Brief description of hero's attraction and love to first wife<br />-Incestuous relationship between Jessie and her father<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Webb was both Ro's downfall, and rise from ashes. Adore how he pulls her out, and brings her spirit to front again.<br />Also heavily adore the breeding undertones of the book! I mean..overuse of word penetration but hell yeah!<br />Wonderful.<br />5/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="9131451058403522829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer6969504028701819183"><br/><b>*** 4<i>Woof</i> Stars***</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390869085i/8293028._SY540_.jpg' width='250' height='290' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><br/><b>Roanna</b> and <b>Jessie</b> are cousins.   <span id="freeText7780566442319621439" style="display:none">I originally read this about 9 years ago when I first found Linda Howard but by now didn't really remember how I felt about it - turns out it's a pretty good story that kept me entertained and even made me cry. There are a few aspects I could have done without - the cousins are a little closer in the family tree than I would like for the leads to be and the graphic descriptions of the taboo relationship with the one character and another person.<br /><br />Overall, a good story with the old Linda Howard mastery of bringing her interesting characters and world to life.</span>

<div id="review_1510291433" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1510291433" />
    <a title="Preeti ♥︎ Her Bookshelves" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves"><img alt="Preeti ♥︎ Her Bookshelves" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467833378p2/32506772.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1510291433?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Preeti ♥︎ Her Bookshelves" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Preeti ♥︎ Her Bookshelves" href="/user/show/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves">Preeti ♥︎ Her Bookshelves</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves?shelf=sibling-cuz-or-bfs-widow-widower">sibling-cuz-or-bfs-widow-widower</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves?shelf=hero-alphahole">hero-alphahole</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves?shelf=evil-bad-guy-or-villain">evil-bad-guy-or-villain</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves?shelf=wrap-it-up-pls">wrap-it-up-pls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves?shelf=hs-virgin-surprise">hs-virgin-surprise</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves?shelf=pregnancy-or-secret-child">pregnancy-or-secret-child</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves?shelf=loved-u-long-or-unrequited">loved-u-long-or-unrequited</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves?shelf=h-wid-doormat-martyr-saint-complex">h-wid-doormat-martyr-saint-complex</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves?shelf=wearing-my-hairshirt-n-loving-it">wearing-my-hairshirt-n-loving-it</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1510291433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9952588932443826326"><br/><br/>I am a huge Linda Howard fan but this book confounded me on so many levels.<br/><br/>The first LH where I dint care much for the h, a highly Mary-sued doormat with a my-emotions-are-in-a-deep-freeze excuse.<br/>The first LH where I dint like the H at all as for all the author’s pushing and prodding, his feelings for the h seemed contrived.<br/>The first LH where the H/h dint work as a couple, at least not till the <i>very</i> end.<br/>The first LH where I couldn’t pinpoint the killer too btw!!<br/>Not the first LH thriller with ick</span>
  <span id="freeText9952588932443826326" style="display:none"><br /><br />I am a huge Linda Howard fan but this book confounded me on so many levels.<br /><br />The first LH where I dint care much for the h, a highly Mary-sued doormat with a my-emotions-are-in-a-deep-freeze excuse.<br />The first LH where I dint like the H at all as for all the author’s pushing and prodding, his feelings for the h seemed contrived.<br />The first LH where the H/h dint work as a couple, at least not till the <i>very</i> end.<br />The first LH where I couldn’t pinpoint the killer too btw!!<br />Not the first LH thriller with icky characters generally spreading their ickiness. But this one took things too bluidy icky far! Seriously ewwww!!<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />The prologue sets the tone for later highly unpleasant-ness. It shows a rich girl enjoying a rough sexual tryst with a pleb kinds for whom she has feelings but is revealed that he doesn't give a damn for her and is only using her for sex. <br /><br />First part opens with the dynamics between three young cousins -one boy and two girls (both recently orphaned)- the H-Webb, the ow-Jessie and the h-Roanna. It’s all about who will be the Davenport heir and also get the house which goes with it-Davencourt. The H/ow are the same age while the h is 7 years younger. The H/ow at 14 are already circling each other sexually and dreaming of inheriting the loot. The h, who imo was the real heir as the only bonafide Davenport was neglected and excluded by one and all, especially the pushy matriarch/grandmother. She plots and pushes the H (her grand nephew) and her spiteful elder granddaughter (the illegitimate daughter of her own beloved daughter of the prologue fame) into a future marriage for which both agree with their own agendas of wealth and power. The bewildered and isolated Roanna gets affection from one person only-Webb and she totally adores him in return. <br /><br />The second part opens 10 years later. The marriage has happened and already in rough loveless waters as the H/ow squabble for sexual and financial control. Roanna, now an awkward skinny 17 years old, still follows Webb around like an exuberant skinny puppy. Now for the gross part- a messed up Jessie knowingly has been having a secret sexual affair with her own father-the guy from the prologue since she was 16. Roanna accidently happens upon them in the present but is scared to tell Webb as she doesn’t want to hurt his feelings. The same day, an everyday affectionate hug heats up between Ro and Webb and Jessie comes upon them and all hell breaks loose. Jessie and Webb have a big row and he storms out saying he wants a divorce. Ro, scared and guilty, thinks of clearing up things with her cousin and goes to her room only to find her bludgeoned to death. An investigation starts with both Ro and Webb as suspects, but both are later cleared. Webb renounces his inheritance and leaves town, hating Ro thinking she deliberately tried to create problems between him and his wife that afternoon. <br /><br />Third part –opens another ten years later and was the most infuriating and exasperating. Even the slippery suspense of catching the killer was barely enough for me to keep reading. The h, now a mother of all Mary Sues grated on my nerves like finger nails on a blackboard. She has turned from a funny clumsy teenager into a quiet unsmiling unassertive shadow of a woman, passably attractive now but with host of psychological problems like anorexia, sleepwalking and loss of confidence. The H is back as she goes and fetches him from Arizona (I think) on her grandmother’s command as only he can save the business. Of course her feelings for the H are still the same and she lets him humiliate her sexually without turning a hair. He redeems himself a bit after that but he was still the irritating interloper to me who dons this mantle of responsibility on sufferance. He talks of throwing out all hangers on relatives (n they have a busloadful of) but then you are one too, buster.<br />And this part was pretty overlong too or so it seemed. I found the first two parts more gripping. Strange as the third part was about the H/h but so much happens and the love/relationship (such as it was) was barely convincing.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The revelation of the actual killer was quite a killer. Only the <i>very end</i> was sweet and gladdening. But still 4 stars for the whole family saga and suspense thing.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9952588932443826326" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15908974452135155297">Linda Howard hit the ball out the park with this one. It had everything that makes for a great read for me. First there is Southern family drama. I am from the South and there is nothing that gives me larger charge than reading about the life, loves and scandal of a family set in the South.<br/><br/>The book is set in two pieces. The first half is all set up. We meet the principle players all at very young, impressionable ages and get a feel for all the intertwined relationships. And then, abruptly, a cha</span>
  <span id="freeText15908974452135155297" style="display:none">Linda Howard hit the ball out the park with this one. It had everything that makes for a great read for me. First there is Southern family drama. I am from the South and there is nothing that gives me larger charge than reading about the life, loves and scandal of a family set in the South.<br /><br />The book is set in two pieces. The first half is all set up. We meet the principle players all at very young, impressionable ages and get a feel for all the intertwined relationships. And then, abruptly, a chain of events that end in a shocking murder. The second half of the book takes place years later and deals with the fallout.<br /><br />What makes this book so good are the gamut emotions that Howard sends her characters through. She rings out every moment of love, angst, betrayal and deceit for maximum effect. And it isn't overwrought or melodramatic at all. It is simply good storytelling.<br /><br />And of course, as this is a Linda Howard book, the sex scenes are steamy and work great in the narrative.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2916054805094801157">I loved this book. I am very fond of romances that start when the hero and heroine are children and we get to see their story over time. This was different and interesting. If you only like one type of story and get squeeked out when the plot has some unsavory elements, you might not like it. I pretty much have a cast iron stomach when it comes to that sort of thing. It's fiction and not only that, the stuff that people object to in this book i.e., incest (not the hero or heroine!) it happens th</span>
  <span id="freeText2916054805094801157" style="display:none">I loved this book. I am very fond of romances that start when the hero and heroine are children and we get to see their story over time. This was different and interesting. If you only like one type of story and get squeeked out when the plot has some unsavory elements, you might not like it. I pretty much have a cast iron stomach when it comes to that sort of thing. It's fiction and not only that, the stuff that people object to in this book i.e., incest (not the hero or heroine!) it happens therefore it's fair game in a fiction book, IMO. I liked how her character developed and how she learned to contain her feelings because she saw how wearing her heart on her sleeve had led to disaster. I have a tendency to like a cool collected heroine anyway and I like it when the hero doesn't really know how she feels and has to work to earn her love. If you liked Dallas and Falcon Crest back in the day, you should love this.</span>

  <span id="freeText4078419748763731152" style="display:none">This was an odd book for me. I was grossed out by the inappropriate (to me any way)relationships in this book. We had second cousins getting married and there was also an even worse couple with a father and daughter. But even with this said, I did like the main couple, Webb and Rowana. I do get why he did, but why, oh why, couldn't these people talk to each other. Had they done that, so many of their problems would have gone away.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1475519899" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8248703918677962187"><b>Author</b>: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16961.Linda_Howard' title='Linda Howard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Linda Howard</a><br/><b>First published</b>: 1996<br/><b>Length</b>: 5392 locations (kindle)<br/><b>Setting</b>: Contemporary.<br/><b>Sex</b>: Explicit. Reasonably frequent.<br/><b>Hero</b>: Rancher / business manager<br/><b>Heroine</b>: Business manager<br/><b>Trigger</b>: Rape. Incest. Murder. Rough sex.<br/><b>Includes</b>: excerpt from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/420733.Kill_and_Tell__CIA_Spies___1_' title='Kill and Tell (CIA Spies, #1) by Linda Howard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kill and Tell</a>.<br/><br/>A clever story but some niggling annoyances.<br/><br/>~ I am uncomfortable with <i>marrying the 2nd cousin</i> especially if they have been brought up in the same household and a childhood crush needs to metamorphose into <i>love</i>.<br/>~ Incest. A difficult topi</span>
  <span id="freeText8248703918677962187" style="display:none"><b>Author</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16961.Linda_Howard" title="Linda Howard" rel="nofollow noopener">Linda Howard</a><br /><b>First published</b>: 1996<br /><b>Length</b>: 5392 locations (kindle)<br /><b>Setting</b>: Contemporary.<br /><b>Sex</b>: Explicit. Reasonably frequent.<br /><b>Hero</b>: Rancher / business manager<br /><b>Heroine</b>: Business manager<br /><b>Trigger</b>: Rape. Incest. Murder. Rough sex.<br /><b>Includes</b>: excerpt from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/420733.Kill_and_Tell__CIA_Spies___1_" title="Kill and Tell (CIA Spies, #1) by Linda Howard" rel="nofollow noopener">Kill and Tell</a>.<br /><br />A clever story but some niggling annoyances.<br /><br />~ I am uncomfortable with <i>marrying the 2nd cousin</i> especially if they have been brought up in the same household and a childhood crush needs to metamorphose into <i>love</i>.<br />~ Incest. A difficult topic to address but it was <i>ugly</i> in this book. And coupled with rough sex it was <i>nasty</i>.<br />~ The ongoing treatment of Roanna, the indifference to her, <i>hurt</i>. And her willingness to keep getting kicked. Even by Webb, made no sense.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[~ The person who killed Jessie kept it secret despite the harm it did others. This <i>never</i> made sense if she was supposed to actually love them. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Overall, it was enjoyable. But it had some issues that niggle after the fact.<br /><br /><b>References</b>:<br />Author on w'pedia: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linda_Howard">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linda_H...</a><br /><br />(ISBN 978-1-439-18791-3)<br /><br />-CR-<br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zahL325VLiRBqQvVOJ0Uim+fREC+cnr7nQqZkm5nefovFiSeepF415pcGITDgFZynJFQ6T8OXXS/pikDZnXQEw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('63Ctj8qnpDJSjE9dsMYQcOrFQoa4glfVGnZAMF2MbAAJzsLO3mPywYl5XAxL21KIGctWLzn+cFo42vChVZ7F6Q==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer234486509001789463"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name.</i><br/><br/>Linda S. Howington is an American best-selling romance author writing under the pseudonym Linda Howard. After 21 years of penning stories for her own enjoyment, she submitted a novel for publication which was very successful. Her first work was published by Silhouette in 1982. She is a charter member of Romance </span>
  <span id="freeText234486509001789463" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name.</i><br /><br />Linda S. Howington is an American best-selling romance author writing under the pseudonym Linda Howard. After 21 years of penning stories for her own enjoyment, she submitted a novel for publication which was very successful. Her first work was published by Silhouette in 1982. She is a charter member of Romance Writers of America and in 2005 Howard was awarded their Career Achievement Award.<br /><br />Linda Howard lives in Gadsden, Alabama with her husband, Gary F. Howington, and two golden retrievers. She has three grown stepchildren and three grandchildren.<br /></span>

        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }
    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>

      </div>

    </div>
